</font></b><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Regulation S-T Rule&nbsp;101(b)(7)&nbsp;only
permits the submission in paper of a Form&nbsp;6-K if submitted to furnish a
report or other document that the registrant foreign private issuer must
furnish and make public under the laws of the jurisdiction in which the
registrant is incorporated, domiciled or legally organized (the registrant&#146;s &#147;home
country&#148;), or under the rules&nbsp;of the home country exchange on which the
registrant&#146;s securities are traded, as long as the report or other document is
not a press release, is not required to be and has not been distributed to the
registrant&#146;s security holders, and, if discussing a material event, has already
been the subject of a Form&nbsp;6-K submission or other Commission filing on
EDGAR.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-indent:1.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">(All
amounts expressed in U.S. dollars unless otherwise noted)</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">AGNICO-EAGLE REPORTS Q3 2009 RESULTS</font></b></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Toronto
(October&nbsp;28, 2009) &#151; Agnico-Eagle Mines Limited</font></b><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">  </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(&#147;Agnico-Eagle&#148; or the &#147;Company&#148;) today reported a quarterly
net loss $17.0 million, or $0.11 per share, for the third quarter of 2009.&#160; This result includes a non-cash foreign
currency translation loss of $22.9 million, or $0.15 per share, as well as
stock option expense of $5.1 million, or $0.03 per share.&#160; Additionally, the result included a gain on
the sale of marketable securities of $5.9 million, or $0.04 per share.&#160; In the third quarter of 2008, the Company
reported net income of $14.0 million, or $0.10 per share.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Cash used in operating activities in the
third quarter of 2009 was $13.8 million, down from cash provided by operating
activities of $17.9 million in the third quarter of 2008.&#160; The impact of significantly higher gold
production, compared to the third quarter of 2008, was more than offset by
changes in working capital largely related to a build-up of material and
supplies inventory at Meadowbank over the summer shipping season, in
anticipation of the mine startup in the first quarter of 2010.&#160; Excluding the large changes in working
capital, cash provided by operating activities increased significantly when
compared to the third quarter of 2008 due to the large increase in gold
revenue.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#147;Agnico-Eagle&#146;s production growth
continues as third quarter gold production increased 73% over the third quarter
of 2008.&#160; However, our production ramp-up
has not been as rapid as we had anticipated which has negatively impacted third
quarter earnings.&#160; We expect a dramatic
improvement in fourth quarter production and cash costs with increased output
at our Kittila and Lapa mines and the ramp-up of production at our Pinos Altos
mine in Mexico&#148;, said Sean Boyd, Vice-Chairman and Chief Executive
Officer.&#160; &#147;Although we have made good
progress resolving start-up issues at our new gold mines, 2009 production
guidance has been reduced to approximately 500,000 ounces.&#160; Additionally, we have decided to build in
additional contingency in our 2010 production forecast as we commission our
remaining new mines.&#160; Our 2010 gold
production forecast is now 1.0 million ounces to 1.1 million ounces, while our
forecasts for 2011 through 2015 remain unchanged&#148;, added Mr.&nbsp;Boyd.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Third quarter 2009 highlights include:</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Solid Cost Control Continues </font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#151; LaRonde, Goldex and Lapa achieve good
minesite cost performance</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Mill start-up at Pinos Altos</font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"> &#151; currently commissioning.&#160; Now producing from mill and heap-leach</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Kittila achieving design
recoveries </font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#151;
the Kittila mill has achieved its design recovery rate of 83% periodically and
has exceeded its design capacity of 3,000 tonnes per day (&#147;tpd&#148;).&#160; Further optimization is ongoing</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Meadowbank Remains On Schedule</font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;"> &#151; Meadowbank remains on schedule for
initial production in the first quarter of 2010.&#160; All necessary construction materials and
consumables are on site</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Symbol" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#183;</font><font size="1" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">LaRonde Extension </font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&#151; shaft sinking almost complete.&#160; Underground development to begin shortly</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-align:left;text-indent:-.25in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Payable gold production(1)&nbsp;in the
third quarter of 2009 was 118,763 ounces at total cash costs per ounce(2)&nbsp;of
$449.&nbsp; This compares with gold production of 68,753 ounces in the third
quarter of 2008 at total cash costs per ounce of $135.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The increase in production, relative to
the third quarter of 2008, is attributable to significantly higher production
from Goldex, as well as production from the Lapa, Kittila and Pinos Altos
mines, which were not in production in that quarter.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The higher cash costs are largely due to
a stronger Canadian dollar and the fact that several of the mines remain in the
start-up/optimization phase and contain no byproduct metals.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the first nine months of 2009,
Agnico-Eagle recorded net income of $38.6 million, or $0.25 per share, down
from the $51.3 million, or $0.36 per share, recorded in the first nine months
of 2008.&#160; Excluding the foreign currency
translation gain and loss recorded in the 2008 and 2009 year to date results
respectively, year to date net income was significantly higher on the strength of
a 76% increase in gold production and stronger gold and base metal prices.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the first nine months of 2009,
Agnico-Eagle had cash provided by operating activities of $61.4 million, down
from $164.5 million in the first nine months of 2008.&#160; The decrease was entirely due to changes in
working capital related to the build-up of gold in inventory at the three new
mines and the buildup of materials and supplies at Meadowbank.&#160; Excluding these working capital changes, cash
provided by operating activities in 2009 increased when compared to the first
nine months of 2008 due to increased metals revenues.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Payable gold production in the first nine
months of 2009 was a record 329,628 ounces at total cash costs per ounce of
$391, up 76% from 187,402 ounces at total cash costs of $15 per ounce in the first
nine months of 2008.&#160; The increase in
production was due to the start-up of the new Kittila, Lapa and Pinos Altos
mines, as well as a production ramp up at Goldex.&#160; The higher cash costs are largely due to a
stronger Canadian dollar and Euro, lower byproduct prices and the fact that
several of the mines remain in the start-up/optimization phase and contain no
byproduct metals.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Full year production is now expected to
be approximately 500,000 ounces of gold.&#160;
The decrease from previous guidance is due to the slower than expected
ramp up of the Kittila mill, the mining of lower grade blocks at Goldex and the
higher than expected ore dilution at the start-up of Lapa.&#160; The early stages of commissioning the plant,
specifically the filter presses in the mill, at Pinos Altos is also taking
longer than expected.&#160; However, as
detailed below, each of these operations made significant progress late in the
third quarter of 2009.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><hr size="1" width="25%" noshade color="black" align="left"></div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(1)&nbsp;Payable production of a mineral
means the quantity of mineral produced during a period contained in products
that are sold by the Company, whether such products are sold during the period
or held as inventory at the end of the period.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(2)&nbsp;Total cash costs per ounce is a
non-GAAP measure.&#160; For reconciliation of
this measure to production costs, as reported in the financial statements, see
Note 1 to the financial statements at the end of this news release.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">2</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">As these operational improvements
continue into the fourth quarter, record quarterly gold production of
approximately 170,000 ounces is expected.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Full year 2010 guidance is reduced to
between 1.0 million ounces and 1.1 million ounces of gold.&#160; The decrease is due to the decision to add a
further contingency to the start-up phase of the new mines based on the
experience in commissioning three new mines in 2009.&#160; However, the long term production forecasts
for these mines remain unchanged.&#160;
Additionally, five internal expansion opportunities have the potential
to further increase the Company&#146;s gold production by more than 50% from 2010
through 2015.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Conference Call Tomorrow</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

conference call on Thursday, October&nbsp;29, 2009 at 11:00&nbsp;a.m.
(E.D.T.).&#160; Management will review the
Company&#146;s financial results for the third quarter 2009 and provide an update of

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Strong Financial
Position Maintained</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Cash and cash equivalents increased to
$239.0 million at September&nbsp;30, 2009 from the June&nbsp;30, 2009 balance
of $173.9 million as cash flow from operations was reinvested largely in
materials, equipment and construction at the Pinos Altos and Meadowbank mine
projects.&#160; In addition, $200 million was
drawn from the Company&#146;s credit lines in the quarter to fund capital
expenditures.&#160; As of September&nbsp;30,
2009, including undrawn credit lines and cash, the Company&#146;s available
liquidity stood at $434 million.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Capital expenditures in the quarter were
$172.8 million, including $90.7 million at Meadowbank, $24.1 million at Pinos
Altos, $21.0 million at Kittila, $20.4 million at LaRonde, $9.9 million at Lapa
and $6.3 million at Goldex.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In 2009, full year capital expenditures
are expected to total approximately $600 million, up $50 million from previous
guidance, reflecting the sharply stronger Canadian dollar and Euro.&#160; During the quarter, the Company realized
proceeds of $34.7 million from the sale of marketable securities.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">3</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Indications are that 2010 capital
expenditures will rise from the previous estimate of approximately $250 million
due to a stronger Canadian dollar and Euro, accelerated development at several
properties, labour and other general cost inflation.&#160; Further detail will be provided in the
Company&#146;s 10 year forecast which will be presented on, or about, December&nbsp;16,
2009.&#160; Included in this update will be
production, capital expenditure and total cash cost guidance as well as the
dividend announcement.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">LaRonde Mine &#151; Continues With
Good Cost Control</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
100% owned LaRonde mine in northwestern Quebec, Canada, began operation in
1988.&#160; Overall, proven and probable gold
reserves at LaRonde total approximately 5.0 million ounces from 35.8 million
tonnes grading 4.3 grams per tonne (&#147;g/t&#148;).&#160;
Life of mine average gold production is expected to be approximately
320,000 ounces per year through 2022.&#160;
First production from the new internal shaft of the LaRonde Extension
remains on schedule for late 2011.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The LaRonde mill processed an average of
6,509 tonnes of ore per day in the third quarter of 2009, compared with an
average of 7,105 tonnes per day in the prior-year period.&#160; The lower production rate was largely a
result of a scheduled seven day shutdown relating to maintenance and upgrades
to the service and production hoist systems at LaRonde.&#160; With a steady-state operation averaging
approximately 7,200 tonnes per day for approximately six years, LaRonde
continues to be a consistent, reliable, world class mine.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Net of byproduct credits, LaRonde&#146;s total
cash costs per ounce were $75 in the third quarter on production of 47,726
ounces of gold.&#160; This compares with the
results of the third quarter of 2008 when total cash costs per ounce were $135
on production of 51,594 ounces of gold.&#160;
The lower gold production in the quarter was largely a result of the
above noted shutdown<b>.</b></font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the first nine months of 2009, LaRonde&#146;s
total cash costs per ounce were $158 on gold production of 157,098 ounces, as
compared to the prior-year period, when the total cash cost per ounce were <i>minus $41 </i>on<i>  </i>production of
161,938 ounces of gold<i>.&#160; </i>The year-over-year increase in
total cash costs is primarily due to the lower realized prices of byproduct
metals. The realized prices for silver, zinc and copper for nine months ending September&nbsp;30,
2009 were 13%, 21% and 33% lower, respectively, compared to the first nine
months of 2008.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Minesite costs per tonne(3)&nbsp;were
approximately C$75 in the third quarter, as expected, compared to C$71 in the
third quarter of 2008.&#160; On a year-to-date
basis, 2009 minesite costs per tonne were C$73, which compares to C$68 in the
prior-year period.&#160; These costs are
higher than the comparable periods in 2008 due to ore stockpile adjustments and
the impact of general cost inflation.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><hr size="1" width="25%" noshade color="black" align="left"></div>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(3)&nbsp;Minesite costs per tonne is a
non-GAAP measure.&#160; For reconciliation of
this measure to production costs, as reported in the financial statements, see
Note 1 to the financial statements at the end of this news release.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">4</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">LaRonde Extension &#151; Shaft Sinking
Nearly Completed</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the third quarter of 2009, shaft
sinking was nearly completed on the new internal shaft, and is within 10 metres
of reaching the final depth of 2,854 metres.&#160;
Changeover to the production installation is expected to start next
month and will be completed before the end of the year.&#160; Preproduction development is scheduled to
start at the beginning of 2010.&#160; The
project is on schedule to start production in late 2011.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Goldex Mine &#151; Already Processing
More Tonnes Than Expected</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Goldex mine in
northwestern Quebec began operation in 2008.&#160;
Proven and probable gold reserves total 1.6 million ounces from 23.8
million tonnes grading 2.1 g/t.&#160; Life of
mine average annual gold production is expected to be approximately 160,000
ounces per year through 2017.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Goldex mine has exceeded the 6,900
tonne per day design capacity for the plant in the third quarter of 2009, with
an average of 7,342 tonnes of ore milled daily.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Third quarter 2009 gold production at
Goldex was 31,169 ounces at total cash costs per ounce of $440.&#160; In the prior-year period, gold production was
17,159 ounces, at total cash costs per ounce of $620, as the mine was ramping
up production.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">For the nine month period ending September&nbsp;30,
2009, total cash costs at Goldex were $379 per ounce on gold production of
102,774 ounces.&#160; There is no corresponding
period in 2008, as the mine achieved commercial production in August&nbsp;2008.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Cost control was very good at Goldex as
minesite costs per tonne were C$22 in the third quarter, compared to C$34 in
the third quarter of 2008.&#160; For the first
nine months of 2009, minesite costs per tonne were C$23.&#160; There is no corresponding period in 2008, as
the mine achieved commercial production in August&nbsp;2008.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Goldex mine gold production is below
expectations for the year due to a decision to focus the mining on the eastern
and central mining blocks, which are lower grade than the overall reserve
grade.&#160; In the meantime, a very large
blast is being prepared for the higher grade western stope.&#160; It was decided to delay mucking this block
and keep it full of broken ore due to rock mechanics considerations.&#160; Normal stope sequencing has resumed with
higher grade ore currently being extracted from the central mining block in October&nbsp;and,
accordingly, gold production is expected to rise in the fourth quarter of 2009.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">At
the present mining and blasting rate, it is expected that the Goldex orebody
will be totally blasted approximately 1.5 years ahead of schedule.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In the second quarter of 2009, an
expansion was announced at Goldex, which is expected to increase the design
production rate from 6,900 tonnes per day to 8,000 tonnes per day.&#160; This project is underway and the new rate is
expected to be achieved by late 2011.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Even
with a plan to expand gold production, Agnico-Eagle expects to extend the mine
life of Goldex. &#160;There are several nearby
zones underground that are likely to be mined.&#160;
They are currently in the resource category and are not included in
reserves.&#160; For example, it is</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">5</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">expected
that the nearby &#147;M&#148; zone will contribute approximately 250,000 ounces of gold
to the overall reserves at Goldex as early as year end 2009, thus increasing
the mine life in spite of the higher planned production rate.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Exploration
is also focused on potentially extending the Goldex orebody to the east and
also on the &#147;S&#148; zone located approximately 100 metres above the current mining
area.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Kittila Mine &#151; Mill Throughput
and Metallurgical Recovery Rates Achieving Design</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Kittila mine in northern
Finland poured its first gold in January&nbsp;2009.&#160; Proven and probable gold reserves total 3.2
million ounces from 21.4 million tonnes grading 4.7 g/t.&#160; Life of mine average gold production is
expected to be approximately 150,000 ounces per year through 2023.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Third quarter 2009 gold production at
Kittila was 18,284 ounces at total cash costs per ounce of $1080.&#160; Minesite costs per tonne at Kittila were
approximately &#128;78 in the third quarter.&#160;
These costs are expected to decline significantly in the fourth quarter
of 2009 as the mine and mill achieve their design rates.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During the third quarter of 2009, the
Kittila mill continued to increase recovery rates and processed an average of
1,958 tonnes per day, versus a design rate of 3,000 tonnes per day, reflecting
the process of optimization.&#160; The mill
had been shut down for 22 days in the quarter, and into early October, largely
due to the replacement of the SAG mill liners, modifications to the CIP circuit
and repairs and maintenance on the autoclave.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Overall gold recoveries were 64% in the
third quarter of 2009 and 70% in September.&#160;
During the third quarter 2009, overall gold recoveries periodically
achieved design rates of 83%.&#160; Recently
in October, the mill has been processing up to 3,300 tonnes per day and is
averaging a 72% recovery rate with some days also achieving 83% recovery.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The open pit mine has been consistently
producing at reserve grade and at a consistent 3,000 tpd over the past two
months, as per design.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A
scoping study is underway examining the possibility of expanding operations at
Kittila.&#160; This plan involves sinking a
shaft on the property combined with an increase in milling capacity.&#160; Results of the study are expected to be
reviewed later this year and will incorporate the most recent exploration
drilling.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Lapa &#151; Optimizing Mining
Cycle</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Lapa mine in northwestern
Quebec began production in April&nbsp;2009.&#160;
Proven and probable gold reserves total 1.1 million ounces from 3.8
million tonnes grading 8.8 g/t.&#160; Life of
mine average gold production is expected to be approximately 115,000 ounces per
year through 2015.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Production from the Lapa mine (all
of which is processed at the LaRonde processing plant) has averaged 1,179
tonnes per day in the third quarter and continues to progress towards&#160; planned design parameters.&#160;&#160; The expected production rate over the life
of the mine is 1,500 tonnes per day and is anticipated to be achieved in the
fourth quarter of 2009.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">6</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='6',FILE='C:\JMS\105732\09-32492-1\task3773070\32492-1-ka-01.htm',USER='105732',CD='Oct 30 02:48 2009' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Third quarter 2009 gold production at
Lapa was 18,409 ounces at total cash costs per ounce of $804, largely as a
result of higher than expected ore dilution in the mining blocks.&#160; These costs are expected to decline
significantly as the mine continues to ramp up towards full production capacity
and the drilling, blasting, excavation and filling cycle are optimized for the
orebody.&#160; Minesite costs per tonne at
Lapa were approximately C$146 in the third quarter, reflecting the higher than
average start-up unit costs often realized in this phase of mining.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Dilution
is currently averaging 57%.&#160; A total of
20 stopes have been extracted from a total of 750 planned.&#160; Efforts to improve dilution include the
implementation of one shot blasting which was found to be very successful at
LaRonde in reducing the mining cycle time.&#160;
A total of four stopes have been mined using this method to date.&#160; Improvements are expected as additional
ground control improvements are implemented and the overall cycle time in each
stope is reduced.&#160; Also, further
optimizations in the Lapa milling circuit are expected to improve recoveries.</font></p>

<p style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Pinos Altos &#151; Plant
Commissioning in Progress</font></b></p>

<p style="background:white;margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Pinos Altos mine in
northern Mexico is now pouring gold from the heap leach and milling
operations.&#160; Proven and probable gold
reserves, including the stand-alone Creston Mascota deposit, total 4.0 million
ounces and 104 million ounces of silver from 41.8 million tonnes grading 2.6
g/t of gold and 72.6 g/t silver.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Life of mine average gold production is
expected to be approximately 170,000 ounces per year through 2028, including
production from Creston Mascota.&#160; Over
this period, annual silver production is expected to average 2.5 million
ounces.&#160; Since the last production
guidance of December&nbsp;11, 2008, the mine life is expected to be increased
by five years due to increased tonnage from drilling, and also from higher gold
and silver prices, which have resulted in additional ore.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
first ore was placed on the leach pads during May&nbsp;2009 and the first gold
bar was poured in July.&#160; Once the project
is in full operation, heap leaching of low grade ores is expected to contribute
approximately 5-10% of the total planned gold production from Pinos Altos.&#160; Gold production in the third quarter of 2009
was 3,175 ounces.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Construction
of the mill at Pinos Altos is now complete and commissioning of the milling
circuit began in September&nbsp;as planned, with ramp up to commercial
operations and design capacity of 4,000 tonnes per day expected in the fourth
quarter of 2009.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">While
commissioning of the tailings filter presses has taken longer than expected,
the mill has already operated at 90% of its designed capacity on some
days.&#160; Recoveries have been according to
plan.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">During
the quarter, 369,320 tonnes of ore containing 19,729 ounces of gold and 335,074
ounces of silver were mined from the Santo Ni&#241;o and Oberon de Weber pits and
4.54 million tonnes of overburden was also mined during the period.&#160; The current ore stockpile contains 690,555
tonnes of ore grading 1.70 g/t of gold and 25.4 g/t of silver, including
211,723 tons of mill grade ore at 3.74 g/t of gold and 52.6 g/t of silver.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">7</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='7',FILE='C:\JMS\105732\09-32492-1\task3773070\32492-1-ka-01.htm',USER='105732',CD='Oct 30 02:48 2009' -->


<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
the underground mine, the two principal ramps were connected on schedule during
August, allowing the development of key infrastructure, production drifts, and
draw points to begin during the fourth quarter.&#160;
Nearly eight kilometres of lateral underground development had been
completed at Pinos Altos by the end of the third quarter.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Approximately
37,000 metres of diamond drilling were completed at the Pinos Altos mine site
and on property-wide exploration in the first half of 2009.&#160; Two surface and two underground diamond
drills were testing deep mine exploration targets at Santo Nino and Cerro
Colorado and expanding the resource on strike and at depth at San Eligio.&#160; Outside the mine-site, three other drills
were exploring the main northern Reyna de Plata structure at El Sinter (where
the Company is contemplating development), testing the Cubiro gold showing in
the western portion of the property, and exploring for extensions of the
Creston Mascota deposit.&#160; Results will be
presented in an upcoming exploration update.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Potential Mill Expansion Being Considered</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The
Company is studying the possibility of increasing the milled production rate at
the main Pinos Altos deposits from 4,000 tonnes per day to 6,000 tonnes per
day, reflecting the 125% increase in reserve tonnage since 2007.&#160; Results of the scoping study are expected by
the third quarter of 2010.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Creston Mascota Approved for Construction &#151; First gold expected early
2011</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">In
July&nbsp;2009, Board approval was received to begin development of Creston
Mascota as a stand-alone satellite heap leach operation.&#160; This deposit is located approximately 12
kilometres from the main Pinos Altos complex.&#160;
Probable reserves at Creston Mascota total approximately 6.7 million
tonnes grading 1.65 g/t gold and 17.1 g/t silver, or approximately 357,000
ounces of gold and 3.7 million ounces of silver.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Basic
engineering and initial site preparations will begin in the fourth quarter of
2009 and are expected to take approximately 18 months to complete.&#160; Production is planned for early 2011 with
annual average production of approximately 48,000 ounces of gold for a mine
life of five years.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Meadowbank Project Remains
on Schedule for Q1, 2010 Start-Up</font></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The 100% owned Meadowbank mine project in
Nunavut, northern Canada, is expected to begin production in the first quarter
of 2010.&#160; Probable gold reserves total
3.6 million ounces from 32.8 million tonnes grading 3.5 g/t.&#160; Life of mine average annual gold production
is expected to be approximately 350,000 ounces through 2019.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Construction
of the new Meadowbank mine project is well advanced.&#160;&#160; Mining from the Portage Pit has been better
than expected with a total of 2.3 million tonnes mined versus 2.0 million
planned.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The waste material from the Portage pit
was used as the main building material in the critical dikes around the
property.&#160; Construction of these dikes
proceeded according to plan.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">8</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

</div>
<!-- SEQ.=1,FOLIO='8',FILE='C:\JMS\105732\09-32492-1\task3773070\32492-1-ka-01.htm',USER='105732',CD='Oct 30 02:48 2009' -->



<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">
<div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Approximately 66,500 tonnes of ore
grading 3.0 g/t are stockpiled.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">All of the material necessary for the
next nine months of operation has now been delivered to the mine site,
including approximately 41,000 tonnes of chemical products and 47 million litres
of fuel.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Approximately 1,050 workers were on the
site during the third quarter of 2009, including 819 construction workers.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The power plant has largely been
completed and pre-commissioning has started.&#160;&#160;
Mechanical installation of both the SAG and ball mills is nearing
completion.&#160; All leach tanks were
completed and mechanical installation is underway.&#160; The remaining process equipment has been
largely installed.&#160; Piping and electrical
installation is approximately 60% complete and will be the focus of remaining
work to be completed prior to start up.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Approximately
27,000 metres of diamond drilling were completed on the Meadowbank
minesite.&#160; An additional 20,500 metres
were completed on exploration targets on the Meadowbank Property.&#160; Results will be featured in an upcoming
exploration press release.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A scoping study is underway which is
considering an increase in the average daily production rate from 8,500 tonnes
per day to 10,000 tonnes per day.&nbsp; This would increase the average annual
gold production to more than 400,000 ounces.&nbsp; The study is currently being
reviewed with Board review expected in the first quarter of 2010.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">About Agnico-Eagle</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Agnico-Eagle is a long established,
Canadian headquartered, gold producer with operations located in Canada, Finland
and Mexico, and exploration and development activities in Canada, Finland,
Mexico and the United States.&#160;
Agnico-Eagle&#146;s LaRonde mine is Canada&#146;s largest operating gold mine in
terms of reserves.&#160; The Company has full
exposure to higher gold prices consistent with its policy of no forward gold
sales.&#160; It has paid a cash dividend for
27 consecutive years.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">9</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Note 1</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Lapa achieved commercial production as of May&nbsp;1, 2009.&#160; Payable production includes commercial
production ounces of 30,013 since May&nbsp;1, 2009; non-commercial production
ounces were nil.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Note 2</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Kittila achieved commercial production as of May&nbsp;1, 2009.&#160; Payable production includes commercial
production ounces of 30,301 since May&nbsp;1, 2009.&#160; Non-commercial production was 6,267 ounces.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Note 3</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Pinos Altos was not in commercial production as of September&nbsp;30,
2009.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><b><u><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Note 4</font></u></b></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Total cash costs per ounce is calculated net of copper, zinc and other
byproduct credits. The weighted average is based on commercial production
ounces.&#160; Total cash costs per ounce is a
non-GAAP measure.&#160; For a reconciliation
to the financial statements, see Note 1 to the financial statements.&#160; See also &#147;Note Regarding Certain Measures of
Performance&#148;</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div style="font-family:Times New Roman;">

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="1" width="25%" noshade color="black" align="left"></div>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(i)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Under the
Company&#146;s revenue recognition policy, revenue is recognized on concentrates
when legal title passes. Since total cash costs are calculated on a production
basis, this inventory adjustment reflects the sales margin on the portion of
concentrate production for which revenue has not been recognized in the&nbsp;period.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(ii)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Total cash costs
per ounce is not a recognized measure under US GAAP and this data may not be
comparable to data presented by other gold producers. The Company believes that
this generally accepted industry measure is a realistic indication of operating
performance and is useful in allowing year over year comparisons. As
illustrated in the table above, this measure is calculated by adjusting
Production Costs as shown in the Consolidated Statements of Income and
Comprehensive Income for net byproduct revenues, royalties, inventory
adjustments and asset retirement provisions. This measure is intended to
provide investors with information about the cash generating capabilities of
the Company&#146;s mining operations. Management uses this measure to monitor the
performance of the Company&#146;s mining operations. Since market prices for gold
are quoted on a per ounce basis, using this per ounce measure allows management
to assess the mine&#146;s cash generating capabilities at various gold prices.
Management is aware that this per ounce measure of performance can be impacted
by fluctuations in byproduct metal prices and exchange rates. Management
compensates for the limitation inherent with this measure by using it in
conjunction with the minesite costs per tonne measure (discussed below) as well
as other data prepared in accordance with US GAAP. Management also performs
sensitivity analyses in order to quantify the effects of fluctuating metal
prices and exchange&nbsp;rates.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(iii)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This inventory
adjustment reflects production costs associated with unsold concentrates.</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt .5in;text-indent:-.5in;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">(iv)</font><font size="1" style="font-size:3.0pt;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160; </font><font size="2" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Minesite costs
per tonne is not a recognized measure under US GAAP and this data may not be
comparable to data presented by other gold producers. As illustrated in the
table above, this measure is calculated by adjusting Production Costs as shown
in the Consolidated Statements of Income and Comprehensive Income for inventory
and asset retirement provisions and then dividing by tonnes processed through
the mill. Since total cash costs data can be affected by fluctuations in
byproduct metal prices and exchange rates, management believes minesite costs
per tonne provides additional information regarding the performance of mining
operations and allows management to monitor operating costs on a more consistent
basis as the per tonne measure eliminates the cost variability associated with
varying production levels. Management also uses this measure to determine the
economic viability of mining blocks. As each mining block is evaluated based on
the net realizable value of each tonne mined, in order to be economically
viable the estimated revenue on a per tonne basis must be in excess of the
minesite costs per tonne. Management is aware that this per tonne measure is
impacted by fluctuations in production levels and thus uses this evaluation
tool in conjunction with production costs prepared in accordance with US GAAP.
This measure supplements production cost information prepared in accordance
with US GAAP and allows investors to distinguish between changes in production
costs resulting from changes in production versus changes in operating
performance.</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">17</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

mining methods, capital costs, total cash costs, minesite costs, and location
of surface infrastructure.&#160; Actual
results and final decisions may be materially different from those currently
anticipated.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Notes To Investors
Regarding The Use Of Resources</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Cautionary Note To
Investors Concerning Estimates Of Measured And Indicated Resources.</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This press
release uses the terms &#147;measured resources&#148; and &#147;indicated resources&#148;. We
advise investors that while those terms are recognized and required by Canadian
regulations, the SEC does not recognize them. <b>Investors
are cautioned not to assume that any part or all of mineral deposits in these
categories will ever be converted into reserves</b>.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Cautionary Note To
Investors Concerning Estimates Of Inferred Resources.</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This press
release also uses the term &#147;inferred resources&#148;. We advise investors that while
this term is recognized and required by Canadian regulations, the SEC does not
recognize it. &#147;Inferred resources&#148; have a great amount of uncertainty as to
their existence, and great uncertainty as to their economic and legal
feasibility. It cannot be assumed that all or any part of an inferred mineral
resource will ever be upgraded to a higher category. Under Canadian rules,
estimates of inferred mineral resources may not form the basis of feasibility
or pre-feasibility studies, except in rare cases. <b>Investors are cautioned not to assume that part or all of an inferred
resource exists, or is economically or legally mineable.</b></font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Scientific And Technical
Data</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">Agnico-Eagle
Mines Limited is reporting mineral resource and reserve estimates in accordance
with the CIM guidelines for the estimation, classification and reporting of
resources and reserves.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Cautionary Note To U.S.
Investors</font></b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">  <b>-</b> The
SEC permits U.S. mining companies, in their filings with the SEC, to disclose
only those mineral deposits that a company can economically and legally extract
or produce. We use certain terms in this press release, such as &#147;measured&#148;, &#147;indicated&#148;,
and &#147;inferred&#148;, and &#147;resources&#148; that the SEC guidelines strictly prohibit U.S.
registered companies from including in their filings with the SEC. U.S.
Investors are urged to consider closely the disclosure in our Form&nbsp;20-F,
which may be obtained from us, or from the SEC&#146;s website at: </font><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">http://sec.gov/edgar.shtml.&#160; A &#147;final&#148;
or &#147;bankable&#148; feasibility study is required to meet the requirements to
designate reserves under Industry Guide 7.&#160;
Estimates were calculated using historic three-year average metals
prices and foreign exchange rates in accordance with SEC Industry Guide 7.&#160; Industry Guide 7 requires the use of prices
that reflect current economic conditions at the time of reserve determination
which Staff of the SEC has interpreted to mean historic three-year average
prices.&#160; The assumptions used for the
mineral reserves and resources estimate reported by the Company on February&nbsp;18th,
2009 were based on three-year average prices for the</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">20</font></p>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">period ending December&nbsp;31,
2008&#160; of $725 per ounce&#160; gold, $13.32 per ounce silver, $1.27 per
pound zinc, $3.15 per pound copper, $0.90 per pound lead and C$/US$, US$/Euro
and MXP/US$ exchange rates of 1.09, 1.37 and 11.00, respectively.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The Canadian
Securities Administrators&#146; National Instrument 43-101 (&#147;NI 43-101&#148;) requires
mining companies to disclose reserves and resources using the subcategories of &#147;proven&#148;
reserves, &#147;probable&#148; reserves, &#147;measured&#148; resources, &#147;indicated&#148; resources and &#147;inferred&#148;
resources. Mineral resources that are not mineral reserves do not have
demonstrated economic viability.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A mineral
reserve is the economically mineable part of a measured or indicated resource
demonstrated by at least a preliminary feasibility study. This study must
include adequate information on mining, processing, metallurgical, economic and
other relevant factors that demonstrate, at the time of reporting, that
economic extraction can be justified. A mineral reserve includes diluting
materials and allows for losses that may occur when the material is mined. A
proven mineral reserve is the economically mineable part of a measured resource
for which quantity, grade or quality, densities, shape and physical
characteristics are so well established that they can be estimated with
confidence sufficient to allow the appropriate application of technical and
economic parameters, to support production planning and evaluation of the
economic viability of the deposit. A probable mineral reserve is the
economically mineable part of an indicated mineral resource for which quantity,
grade or quality, densities, shape and physical characteristics can be
estimated with a level of confidence sufficient to allow the appropriate
application of technical and economic parameters, to support mine planning and
evaluation of the economic viability of the deposit.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A mineral
resource is a concentration or occurrence of natural, solid, inorganic or
fossilized organic material in or on the Earth&#146;s crust in such form and
quantity and of such a grade or quality that it has reasonable prospects for
economic extraction. The location, quantity, grade, geological characteristics
and continuity of a mineral resource are known, estimated or interpreted from
specific geological evidence and knowledge. A measured mineral resource is that
part of a mineral resource for which quantity, grade or quality, densities,
shape and physical characteristics can be estimated with a level of confidence
sufficient to allow the appropriate application of technical and economic
parameters, to support mine planning and evaluation of the economic viability
of the deposit. The estimate is based on detailed and reliable exploration,
sampling and testing information gathered through appropriate techniques from
locations such as outcrops, trenches, pits, workings and drill holes that are
spaced closely enough to confirm both geological and grade continuity. An
indicated mineral resource is that part of a mineral resource for which
quantity, grade or quality, densities, shape and physical characteristics can
be estimated with a level of confidence sufficient to allow the appropriate
application of technical and economic parameters, to support mine planning and
evaluation of the economic viability of the deposit. The estimate is based on
detailed and reliable exploration and testing information gathered through
appropriate techniques from locations such as outcrops, trenches, pits,
workings and drill holes that are spaced closely enough for geological and
grade continuity to be reasonably assumed. An inferred mineral resource is that
part of a mineral resource for which quantity and grade or quality can be
estimated on the basis of geological evidence and limited sampling and
reasonably assumed, but not verified, geological and grade continuity. The
estimate is based on limited information and sampling gathered through
appropriate techniques from locations such as outcrops, trenches, pits,
workings and drill</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">21</font></p>

<div style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;"><hr size="3" width="100%" noshade color="#010101" align="left"></div>

</div>

<br clear="all" style="page-break-before:always;">


<div>

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">holes. Mineral
resources which are not mineral reserves do not have demonstrated economic
viability.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Investors are cautioned
not to assume that part or all of an inferred resource exists, or is
economically or legally mineable.</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">A feasibility
study is a comprehensive study of a mineral deposit in which all geological,
engineering, legal, operating, economic, social, environmental and other
relevant factors are considered in sufficient detail that it could reasonably
serve as the basis for a final decision by a financial institution to finance
the development of the deposit for mineral production.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">The mineral
reserves presented in this disclosure are separate from and not a portion of
the mineral resources.</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

information can be found in the Company&#146;s press release dated December&nbsp;11,

<p align="center" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:center;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><b><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;font-weight:bold;">Note Regarding Certain
Measures Of Performance</font></b></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">&nbsp;</font></p>

<p align="left" style="margin:0in 0in .0001pt;text-align:left;"><font size="2" face="Times New Roman" style="font-size:10.0pt;">This press
release presents measures including &#147;total cash costs per ounce&#148; and &#147;minesite
costs per tonne&#148; that are not recognized measures under US GAAP. This data may
not be comparable to data presented by other gold producers. The Company
believes that these generally accepted industry measures are realistic
indicators of operating performance and useful for year-over-year comparisons.
However, both of these non-GAAP measures should be considered together with
other data prepared in accordance with US GAAP, these measures, taken by
themselves, are not necessarily indicative of operating costs or cash flow
measures prepared in accordance with US GAAP.&#160;
The Company provides a reconciliation of realized total cash costs per
ounce and minesite costs per tonne to the most comparable US GAAP measures in
its annual and interim filings with securities regulators in Canada and the
United States.&#160; A reconciliation of the
Company&#146;s total cash costs per ounce and minesite costs per tonne to the most
comparable financial measures calculated and presented in accordance with US
GAAP for the Company&#146;s historical results of operations is set out in Note 1 to
the financial statements included herein.</font></p>
